  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer11715281757619545098">Past midnight, Chyna Shepard, twenty-six, gazes out a moonlit window, unable to sleep on her first night in the Napa Valley home of her best friend's family. Instinct proves reliable. A murderous sociopath, Edgler Foreman Vess, has entered the house, intent on killing everyone inside.   <span id="freeText11715281757619545098" style="display:none">Past midnight, Chyna Shepard, twenty-six, gazes out a moonlit window, unable to sleep on her first night in the Napa Valley home of her best friend's family. Instinct proves reliable. A murderous sociopath, Edgler Foreman Vess, has entered the house, intent on killing everyone inside. A self-proclaimed "homicidal adventurer," Vess lives only to satisfy all appetites as they arise, to immerse himself in sensation, to live without fear, remorse or limits, to live with "intensity." Chyna is trapped in his deadly orbit. <br /><br />Chyna is a survivor, toughened by a lifelong struggle for safety and self-respect. Now she will be tested as never before. At first her sole aim is to get out alive--until, by chance, she learns the identity of Vess's next intended victim, a faraway innocent only she can save. Driven by a newly discovered thirst for meaning beyond mere self-preservation, Chyna musters every inner resource she has to save an endangered girl...as moment by moment, the terrifying threat of Edgler Foreman Vess intensifies.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10064716?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alejandro" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alejandro" href="/user/show/665584-alejandro">Alejandro</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/665584-alejandro?shelf=novel">novel</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10064716" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3660215132155075550"><b>
  <u>Intense!!! All right!!!</u>
</b><br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>PERFECT TITLE</u>
</b><br/><br/>The title for this novel, <i>Intensity</i>...<br/><br/>...is truly well selected since this book is indeed...<br/><br/>...<b>intense!!!</b><br/><br/>You are barely getting confortable, starting to read the book, just a few pages, when...<br/><br/><b>Bam! Kapow! Tomá guacho!</b><br/><br/>The horror begins!<br/><br/>So, if you are a horror novel where you don't have to wait much to be full immersed in the action, don't look anymore! This is it! You found the book!<br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>NOT FOR THE FAINT OF HEART</u>
</b><br/><br/>I have read quite several books by Koontz</span>
  <span id="freeText3660215132155075550" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>Intense!!! All right!!!</u>
</b><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>PERFECT TITLE</u>
</b><br /><br />The title for this novel, <i>Intensity</i>...<br /><br />...is truly well selected since this book is indeed...<br /><br />...<b>intense!!!</b><br /><br />You are barely getting confortable, starting to read the book, just a few pages, when...<br /><br /><b>Bam! Kapow! Tomá guacho!</b><br /><br />The horror begins!<br /><br />So, if you are a horror novel where you don't have to wait much to be full immersed in the action, don't look anymore! This is it! You found the book!<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>NOT FOR THE FAINT OF HEART</u>
</b><br /><br />I have read quite several books by Koontz and...<br /><br />...I was shocked by the crudity of the very first scenes. <br /><br />I told myself (back then in 2007): "Dang! He (Koontz) is not fooling around! The villain, in this novel, is truly a grim, dark and twisted sonofa...". <br /><br />Another of the most shocking things in this book, since you don't have any paranormal/sci-fi elements here (that's an usual trait by Koontz), all the horror here is made by somebody that it's quite "just" a human being...<br /><br />...but don't fool yourself, since the villain here can scare more than the fiercest demon that you may encounter in other novel. <br /><br />Even when you think that you can't get surprised anymore by him...<br /><br />...<b>wrong!</b><br /><br />You'll get even more surprised...<br /><br />...oh, yes...<br /><br />... and even more afraid.<br /><br />Trust me.<br /><br />You'll meet true evil, truly human.<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>BOLD HEROINE</u>
</b><br /><br />And since you have a really scary bad man...<br /><br />...the only fair thing is to have a really awesome great woman.<br /><br />I like the heroine here since I think that she acted in very logical way and every action that she does is well motivated and reasoned.<br /><br />She doesn't have special skills like martial arts or anything, but she certainly have guts, have brains, and have common sense. <br /><br />The story actually has very few characters beyond the villain and the heroine, but still you will have plenty of reading, plenty of development,...<br /><br />...plenty of intensity!!!<br /><br />Brace yourself!<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3660215132155075550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60696699" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60696699" />
    <a title="Norm de Plume" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2043075-norm-de-plume"><img alt="Norm de Plume" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603573047p2/2043075.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60696699?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norm de Plume" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norm de Plume" href="/user/show/2043075-norm-de-plume">Norm de Plume</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer60696699&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60696699" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer743969373362036450">I hate Dean Koontz, but I go through books quickly and have to have something to read at work, and when it comes down to it, I'll read anything you put in front of me even if it's bad just for something to do. Allegedly, this was one of his better books. The best book I've read of his, I would give two stars. Don't even remember what it was called. It pains me that this man is the second best selling author in the US. Seriously.<br/><br/>Why? Well, where to begin? Let's start with characters. Dean Koontz </span>
  <span id="freeText743969373362036450" style="display:none">I hate Dean Koontz, but I go through books quickly and have to have something to read at work, and when it comes down to it, I'll read anything you put in front of me even if it's bad just for something to do. Allegedly, this was one of his better books. The best book I've read of his, I would give two stars. Don't even remember what it was called. It pains me that this man is the second best selling author in the US. Seriously.<br /><br />Why? Well, where to begin? Let's start with characters. Dean Koontz doesn't create characters; he just creates caricatures. The main characters stories of childhood trauma aren't remotely believable. If her mother didn't give a shit about her and was constantly moving around, why would she even bother to bring her for 16 years? Everything is so extreme in her character that there's never any remotely realistic motivation for any of it. The villain is concerned only with <i>intensity</i>, mostly written in italics, because italics are apparently <i>intense</i>. His philosophy is that any <i>intense</i> experience is worthwhile. Basically, he should be on the X-Games doing flips on motorcycles and appearing in Mountain Dew commercials. The way Koontz beats the shit out of the <i>intensity</i> motif, I find it hard to believe more people aren't rolling their eyes and saying, "Gimme a break."<br /><br />How about his craft? Clunky, uninspired, repetitious prose with awful dialogue. I don't remotely understand why people buy this guy's books. There is nothing compelling about his craft. For a guy they call "The Master of Suspense", he lacks all sense of subtlety. He constantly holds the reader's hand unnecessarily as if afraid they won't get it any time he uses some kind of symbolism. Not that it's common with Koontz. He's always saying more than is necessary and it gets a little insulting over time, as if he thinks his readers are so stupid they can't possibly pick up on the things he's writing without help.<br /><br />So, his plots must be super-awesome to make up for it all, right? Let's face it; with most pulp, people don't give a shit how it's written. They only care about the story. This story is about some chick who goes to a friend's for the weekend, only to have the entire friend's family killed and end up the sole survivor riding along with the killer, trying to come up with a way to take him down and save some girl she's never met that the killer has locked in his basement. The upside of this story is most of it leaves the heroine alone, so you're not subjected to the cringe-worthy dialogue that the book opens with. It also means that Dean Koontz has to find some way to create his particular breed of melodrama through sometimes very slow events, so he prattles on for pages about a cramp in the heroine's ass, or she freaks out talking about how she will surely sustain a grievous spinal injury by slamming the chair she's chained to into the stone fireplace wall by backing into it. Every time she takes a whack at it, "OHHHHHHH GOD THE PAIN IT HURTS SOOOOOOO BAAAAAAAD!" Gimme a fucking break. It's make of PINE. Fuck you, Dean, it's not dramatic that you have no grasp of physics whatsoever. Half of this book is her considering a fairly simple action and then contemplating the multitude of ways it could go horribly wrong and leave her critically injured. There's no real drama and nothing to care about, so Dean Koontz tries to manufacture some by telling you how you should feel about what she's doing.<br /><br />I can't even begin to convey how inane this book truly is. Hopefully I've given you some idea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="743969373362036450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1606194354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1606194354" />
    <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn"><img alt="Skyler Autumn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534857879p2/12859342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1606194354?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Skyler Autumn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Skyler Autumn" href="/user/show/12859342-skyler-autumn">Skyler Autumn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1606194354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer741237418893342235"><b>3 Stars</b><br/><br/>Chyna is taken to her best friend's family home for a mini break during the school year only to spend the first night hidden under the guest bed as a home invader proceeds to murder all the occupants. Having both an unusual and terrifying childhood Chyna has developed a skill set that has made her a survivor both then and now. As she peers out the window of the guest bedroom she hears a muffled scream and creaking footsteps heading towards her room, instinct takes over and she is under th</span>
  <span id="freeText741237418893342235" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars</b><br /><br />Chyna is taken to her best friend's family home for a mini break during the school year only to spend the first night hidden under the guest bed as a home invader proceeds to murder all the occupants. Having both an unusual and terrifying childhood Chyna has developed a skill set that has made her a survivor both then and now. As she peers out the window of the guest bedroom she hears a muffled scream and creaking footsteps heading towards her room, instinct takes over and she is under the bed, and out of sight. Chyna is fully aware that the bed has not been slept in and her things are safely hidden in the closet so that the room appears unused and hopefully the intruder will move on. <br /><br />Edward Vess lives life intensely his senses are primed for optimal absorbance. He basks in both pain and pleasure and believes to live without fear is too truly embrace life. Tonight like many nights before he has entered a home that is not his and plans to kill everyone inside. <br /><br />This novel started out exactly as advertised In-FUCKING-Tensity. I read this book alone at night and found myself startled at every little noise thinking Edward Vess was in my home. It was eery and terrifying and you couldn't help wonder how you would react thrusted into a similar life threatening situation. I know one thing I'd do for sure, is stay in the house after the killer leaves, count my lucky stars I wasn't discovered by him and then immediately call the police because I, unlike Chyna, am not a crazy person!<br /><br />The first 30% of the novel I was immersed and you would have to pry the book out of my cold dead hands to stop me from reading it, but then the author took the readers out of the claustrophobia and tension that was the home, into a road trip, into other environments and unfortunately out of the part of the story I was enjoying so immensely. <br /><br />It took me so far out of the novel because our protagonist has now gone from survivor to Rose McGowan in Scream trying to escape the killer through a doggy door.... like really?? WHAT ARE YOU DOING IDIOT!! The protagonist began to make poor decision after poor decision and even though the author tried to explain it a way with thin ass logic, as a reader I was left with the running inner dialogue of: WHAT ARE YOU DOING IDIOT!?<br /><br />Also weirdly enough for someone like myself who LOVES reading inside the mind of a serial killer I actually didn't care for it in this novel. I wanted to be completely in the dark on where the killer was and what he was doing, thinking, and feeling but instead I got to know exactly where his head was at all times which took away from the creepy suspense. I'd rather of had this entire novel in the protagonist perspective instead of jumping back and forth. I think it would have made me a lot more unnerved by just the plain unknowing. I would be left with the same frantic question of; did he spot her? But instead I always knew the answer to that question which brought down the intensity of the novel. <br /><br />Overall I like Dean Koontz, I went into this novel thinking he'd be like trashy Urban Fantasy writing but it was full of such deep descriptions, complex characters and vivid imagery. This novel was dark and not at all light and fluffy as I originally suspected. Although I didn't love this novel I really would like to read more Dean Koontz in my future. If you like'd this novel may I suggest You're Next a great horror film with survivalist girl as the lead (#GIRLPOWER); I'd also recommend High Tension but it is a well known plagiarism of this book and other then the different endings it is basically a carbon copy of Dean Koontz, and I don't support people who steal other's creative property.</span>
  <a data-text-id="741237418893342235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2802130159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2802130159" />
    <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf"><img alt="Cody | CodysBookshelf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592500568p2/56352820.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2802130159?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody | CodysBookshelf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody | CodysBookshelf" href="/user/show/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf">Cody | CodysBookshelf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679425250" href="/book/show/64958.Intensity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56352820-cody-codysbookshelf?shelf=dean-koontz">dean-koontz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2802130159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13718875606404103910">Ask any Dean Koontz fan what their favorite Koontz book is, and the answer you will likely get is <i>Watchers</i>, or maybe <i>Odd Thomas</i>. Exceptions to this exist, of course, but those two titles seem to get the most love amongst his fanbase. <br/><br/>Personally, my favorite was <i>The City</i> . . . Until I read <i>Intensity</i>.<br/><br/>This novel is really quite unlike most everything else by Koontz . . . unlike what I’ve read by him, anyway. There is no cloying sentimentality. No precocious children, no forced romance (Koontz almos</span>
  <span id="freeText13718875606404103910" style="display:none">Ask any Dean Koontz fan what their favorite Koontz book is, and the answer you will likely get is <i>Watchers</i>, or maybe <i>Odd Thomas</i>. Exceptions to this exist, of course, but those two titles seem to get the most love amongst his fanbase. <br /><br />Personally, my favorite was <i>The City</i> . . . Until I read <i>Intensity</i>.<br /><br />This novel is really quite unlike most everything else by Koontz . . . unlike what I’ve read by him, anyway. There is no cloying sentimentality. No precocious children, no forced romance (Koontz almost goes there in the final chapter, but he redeems himself), no cornball military men or bougainvillea or wacky spirituality or Goldens. Just a sympathetic, kick-ass protagonist and the scariest, most loathsome villain Koontz has put to paper. And the only dogs to appear on the narrative are taken care of in a . . . well, rather un-Koontz-like fashion.<br /><br />What is on display here is Koontz’s marvelous plotting skill: making a story move <i>this</i> well takes some serious chops. From the first page to the last I was enthralled, horrified. I’m not used to Koontz scaring me so badly, but he did it here.<br /><br />Okay, enough with my fanboying. I’m just happy, okay? It’s been a while since I last read a Koontz novel I <b>love</b> so hard. I’m kicking myself for being aware of this book for a decade or longer, yet only reading it now. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13718875606404103910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3987594870654101159">I have never read a more action packed book in my life. It never once let up - almost from page one.   <span id="freeText3987594870654101159" style="display:none">I have never read a more action packed book in my life. It never once let up - almost from page one. In some ways it was a little disorienting because you never had a moment to breathe, but at the same time that's also what you really want when you read a thriller. The writing was meh, nothing special. But the story itself was skillfully told. And obviously unsettling. You get in the head of a serial killer, and who really wants to spend any time in that place!? Not me. And yet, I read the whole book in two days. The book was very aptly named: it was intense. And thrilling.<br /><br />Also, the main character makes really dumb decisions. So...just know that going in.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296859710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10014229604208338639">The last 200 pages of this book are what makes me want to give it 5 stars but I didn't enjoy it as much as I hoped to, so four stars it is. The end plot twist was something I did not see coming and for that I applaud Koontz; I read this book relatively quickly and I didn't have to force myself to keep reading. </span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=audible-books">audible-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5230033-karen-b?shelf=koontz">koontz</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159144588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17746143823403985928">Re reading for September 2015 with Koontzland group. As with many Koontz novels, I enjoyed this one more the second time around. First of all I liked Koontz' descriptions, vivid but not too long. His use of simile and metaphor enhanced the reading for me. I won't go into the plot because many other reviewers have done that. As for characterization, Chyna is one of Koontz' strongest female characters. She fought for herself as a young girl and continues to fight the obstacles in her path. Chyna i</span>
  <span id="freeText17746143823403985928" style="display:none">Re reading for September 2015 with Koontzland group. As with many Koontz novels, I enjoyed this one more the second time around. First of all I liked Koontz' descriptions, vivid but not too long. His use of simile and metaphor enhanced the reading for me. I won't go into the plot because many other reviewers have done that. As for characterization, Chyna is one of Koontz' strongest female characters. She fought for herself as a young girl and continues to fight the obstacles in her path. Chyna is as intense in her determination to free herself and another as Edgler Vess is in his attempt to spread destruction. For Edgler (love the use of the "d" in his name as he points out that he is on the "edge") what matters is sensation. He has synesthesia (described in the book) the ability to observe with more than one sense. ex - taste colors) He is about the sensation of whatever he does. The feel, the taste, the smell, the sound of whatever he does including his murders. All of life for him is about sensation. Chyna pushes herself physically and in doing so builds an interior strength that keeps her going. She is about living and living UNHARMED. There are really just the two characters, Chyna and Vess and it is a battle Koontz often explores in his novels ... between good and evil.<br /><br /> Update June 2017<br />This was a re-read for me this time and I enjoyed it just as much as the first time. Koontz has a way of describing the dark side of human nature that you know even though this is fiction, human depravity is out there and there will always be those who find inner strength to fight it in one way or another. A lot of Chyna's victory in this novel is finding that inner strength as she struggles with herself.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17746143823403985928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15144684600541930113">I decided that I would write a little about the books that I finish for now on. This was a very scary story! I have to say that it actually scared me sometimes and that is pretty hard to do. "Intensity" is a very appropriate title for this book, I couldn't stay away from it. Definately a plesant surprise after reading Dean Koontz's "Life Expectancy". This book never let up on it's suspense from beginning to end. If anyone is looking for a good horror, "Intensity" fits the bill. Be warned though,</span>
  <span id="freeText15144684600541930113" style="display:none">I decided that I would write a little about the books that I finish for now on. This was a very scary story! I have to say that it actually scared me sometimes and that is pretty hard to do. "Intensity" is a very appropriate title for this book, I couldn't stay away from it. Definately a plesant surprise after reading Dean Koontz's "Life Expectancy". This book never let up on it's suspense from beginning to end. If anyone is looking for a good horror, "Intensity" fits the bill. Be warned though, this book has a lot of adult stuff and has a lot of situations that are difficult to swallow as the story is centered around the actions of a sociopath and depicts instances of severe child abuse. However, I gave it five stars becuase I couldn't put it down, it kept me guessing, and it was actually scary and not cheesy like many horror novels. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1135498812" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16131877431914568715">I think I have sadly hit my limit with Koontz. My first book by this author was AMAZING. The second was just as amazing. Then somewhere down the road, the villains all started to meld together. The villains became a little predictable for me because they all shared the same qualities. <br/><br/><br/><i>Now that doesn't mean that this book didn't entertain me.</i> There were times that my heart was racing and I was scared to death for the MC. The first 60% of the book was the best. I just wanted it to be over after th</span>
  <span id="freeText16131877431914568715" style="display:none">I think I have sadly hit my limit with Koontz. My first book by this author was AMAZING. The second was just as amazing. Then somewhere down the road, the villains all started to meld together. The villains became a little predictable for me because they all shared the same qualities. <br /><br /><br /><i>Now that doesn't mean that this book didn't entertain me.</i> There were times that my heart was racing and I was scared to death for the MC. The first 60% of the book was the best. I just wanted it to be over after that point. To be honest, I sped read the rest. I predicted everything that happened, which is bad because I can't predict much of anything. <b> I make it a point to not look ahead during a story, but the plot in <i>Intensity</i> slapped me square in the face. </b><br /><br /><br />If you enjoy thrillers and haven't read many (or any) Koontz novels, then you will probably love <i>Intensity</i>. My first and favorite Koontz novels <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32424.Lightning" title="Lightning by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">Lightning</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32441.The_Good_Guy" title="The Good Guy by Dean Koontz" rel="nofollow noopener">The Good Guy</a>. <br /><br /><br />I'm giving this 3 stars because I loved the first 60%. I'm still going to give Odd Thomas a go later on, but I think I'm done with his other novels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16131877431914568715" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3204697487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3204697487" />
    <a title="Fonch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8647009-fonch"><img alt="Fonch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1333994582p2/8647009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3204697487?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fonch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fonch" href="/user/show/8647009-fonch">Fonch</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3204697487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer826945942132294471"> Ladies and gentlemen I surprisingly managed to end my criticism of "Linnea Hartsuyker's"The Half-DrownedKing," but as I warned when drafting the above-mentioned review. It is quite possible that I will not be able to finish the criticism quoted today, and I am forced to continue it tomorrow, so I ask Goodreads users to be patient with me.<br/>What surprised me as I read Dean R. Koontz's novel is the huge number of people. That is, users, who followed with great interest the reading progress of"Inten</span>
  <span id="freeText826945942132294471" style="display:none"> Ladies and gentlemen I surprisingly managed to end my criticism of "Linnea Hartsuyker's"The Half-DrownedKing," but as I warned when drafting the above-mentioned review. It is quite possible that I will not be able to finish the criticism quoted today, and I am forced to continue it tomorrow, so I ask Goodreads users to be patient with me.<br />What surprised me as I read Dean R. Koontz's novel is the huge number of people. That is, users, who followed with great interest the reading progress of"Intensity". I do not think frankly, that my criticism may arouse so much interest, but from the heart, but I heartily thank all the goodreads users, who expressed their interest in the progress of this novel.<br />Although I don't think, this criticism i was completely pleased with. I found it regular, although it got better as I approached the end. The first thing I should note is a curiosity, or anecdote, and that is that in the wake of the coronavirus crisis in Wuhan China. Dean Koontz has become very famous, because as I said, and I noted in my review "The Half-Drowned King"in his novel"The Eye of Darkness" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32443.The_Eyes_of_Darkness?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=dsW7Fn5J5B&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3...</a> <br />he prophesied, an epidemic of an unknown disease would appear in Wuhan. The first thing I must say is that, although I do not know Dean R. Koontz as a collector of Catholic writers, I was immensely pleased with his success and I hope, this blessed chance. I helped republish his works (something that is happening because on Friday I went to see bookstores and found his new book in Spanish <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.todostuslibros.com/libros/la-habitacion-de-los-susurros_978-84-9187-225-2">https://www.todostuslibros.com/libros...</a> by the way do not much heed a publishing house that has written the Country about him)<br />, and those that are still unpublished in Spanish. Koontz generally generates distrust of governments that wield power absolutely. You could say, you subscribe to Lord Acton's quote <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/969937.John_Emerich_Edward_Dalberg_Acton">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <br />that "Power corrupts, and absolute power absolutely corrupts" and this show of dissatisfaction is shown by the number of political leaders who have emerged prompting the rejection of the majority (not you who think), precisely those you do not think of. We certainly do not know what they are proposing or the power that certain lobbyists have over them, so I say, that I do not believe, that it is precisely the common good. But the satisfaction of inbreds. and this show of dissatisfaction is shown by the number of political leaders who have emerged, prompting the rejection of the majority (not those you think), precisely those of those you do not think of. We certainly do not know what they are proposing or the power that certain lobbyists have over them, so I say, that I do not believe, that it is precisely the common good. But the satisfaction of inbreds. Since Koontz has become an improvised prophet. I'm going to give my own opinion, on the subject of coronavirus (don't worry I won't steal too much time from you, because I didn't forget what I have to talk about that's from "Intensity"). I can only show my agreement with Don Juan Manuel de Prada (as always). The first thing is to denounce the enormous cowardice of today's society. It has been noted that these aggressions that came from the modern world, nominalism, rebirth, Protestantism, liberalism, and illustration. They have shown us that there is no need to believe in God, and that science will solve all our problems. Oy as Father Brown said in the "Resurrection of Father Brown" in "Father Brown's Disbelief" that God gives us wisdom, and common sense <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/184594.The_Incredulity_of_Father_Brown?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=NEGMd0YGvS&amp;rank=2">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> The attacks by the currents I have denounced have led us to believe that there is only one thing, and it is this earthly life. It is no longer believed in what catechism calls life after death. As the gurus of atheism say (I do not intend to fall for their tactics of insulting them, even if they are very good, especially Mr Onfray). Both Mr. Dawkins, and the deceased Hitchens, Harris, Denet, Comte Sponville, and Mr. Pullman, especially the latter have it very clear or man when he dies is a set of atoms that dissolves, or as a certain gnostic politician says, without him you must know that you should storm the heavens and be a God. The maxim of Peak of The Looking, that man is either the worst of animals, or something close to divinity there is nothing invented <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/134145.Giovanni_Pico_della_Mirandola">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> (this has generated a current called Transhumanism that Bostrom and others support, who believes that man due to genetic modification and cybernetics will not know death, as a colleague of my father said, and the Aquinate "there is no infinite progress in a finite world" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/158904.Thomas_Aquinas">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a># on this subject I recommend Gustave Thibon's book <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1613776.Gustave_Thibon">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a># edited by Father Cervera in the Publisher Didaskalos with prologue by my admirated Juan Manuel de Prada <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/244771.Juan_Manuel_de_Prada">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> This man Thibon was called by the <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/275648.Socrates?from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> . They'll see why. The book is called "You will be like gods" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.editorialdidaskalos.org/libro/sereis-como-dioses_105585/">https://www.editorialdidaskalos.org/l...</a> i also recommend you of Didaskalos <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28204354-the-global-sexual-revolution">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a> ). This by respecting the primal temptation of you will be like gods. This has already been loaded by the coronavirus, for the science that shows us that God does not exist. It cannot, as my admired Prada says, do anything against Coronavirus, and since this is a utilitarian society in which only what one can give matters, and incapacity is not tolerated and sickness proceeds to use programs that prevent us from suffering. I admit that I do not agree with therapeutic incarnation, but life is not always pleasures, and amusements. There are times when things don't go our way. Suffering shows us how Dostoyevsky, C.S. Lewis, and G.K. Chesterton already foretold, bringing us closer to God for it sometimes it is necessary for <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3137322.Fyodor_Dostoyevsky">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1069006.C_S_Lewis">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7014283.G_K_Chesterton">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a>. We saw it in the Lovely Bones adaptation that the important thing is not eternal life, but this one. Hence, as Christopher Dawson pointed out brilliantly in a booklet, he edited Encounter. Expensive, but worth its weight in gold "The Gods of Revolution" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22725471-the-gods-of-revolution">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a> when Kaunitz one of the pioneers of illustration in Austria. Minister of Archduchess Teresa of Habsburg, when it was his account to God, he was afraid to live. These modern heresies have taught us how to live, but not how to die. Yet for now it is this system that has triumphed, and the lords I mentioned above who have shaped our world. In such a way that the scientist Carlos Alberto Marmelada friend of my admired Manuel Alfonseca points out <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1117598.Manuel_Alfonseca">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> in his book "The God of Atheists" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25607487-el-dios-de-los-ateos?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=vHRPqlHrFe&amp;rank=5">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a> we live in a world of religious helplessness. God exists, but I act, as if he didn't exist. That is why it is very common the non-practising Catholic, who, as the priest of a town where he spent the summer, said is like saying an athlete who does not run, or a bullfighter who does not bully. In general this is the situation of Western society living in a religious indifferentism with his back to God, with a slight anti-clericalism, even if militant atheists courtesy of the lords mentioned above are increasingly making noise. More than atheism (although there are also) what predominates is an anti-Christianity motivated by the elites, if someone overdoes it and wants to go further as Dawkins is called to order the enemy is Christianity this already realized G.K. Chesterton in his book book "The Sphere and the Cross" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259052.The_Ball_and_the_Cross?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=16twT5IUZa&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a>. People are receptive to this philosophy, but they don't dare make the leap. It is then that something escapes this conception, and something like the coronavirus appears, which shows us our earthly nature. The first thing I'll say, don't worry, sui is a nuisance, and people are dying, but coronavirus is not the black plague, or septicaemics, not even syphilis, and AIDS. So, that calms down, and very careful, with what the news says. You have to take precautions, of course. But don't let us panic. If someone is sick, go to the doctor, and they are insulated. Don't let people see him as a monster. But with a human being, who has a disease, but with the dignity of being a child of God. Perhaps one of the flaws of, De Prada (although you have not yet given you time to talk to us about the subject) are the consequences , but not what should be done <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3063220.Thomas_More">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> I see the coronavirus, as an opportunity, to bring out the best, which we all carry within, to do the greatest good to our neighbour. Instead of running scared, let us reflect, and act with kindness. Let us accompany the sick where versily, and provide them with the material, and spiritual support they need. Let's act like a team all together. Let us not behave like the heathen of Nero's time with the fire of Rome, but as the Christians of Quo Vadis <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/538845.Quo_Vadis?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=IxfnPXbHNV&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5...</a> Lead a normal life, and don't be infected by alarmism. Even if the worst were to happen, know that death is not the end, and that behind it is eternal life, or the abode of the Father. Of course, what I have said does not prevent us from being cared for. It's good to close the rubbents until the outbreak. Especially not criminalizing. The Chinese are not to blame, and that our anger does not fall upon them. That, let us recognize that this human shredder called communism has not been up to the task. I hope, this crisis i conscientious against its evils. Look, that capitalism is no better, and that advocated for a third way the distributionism inspired by the Social Doctrine of the Church. I'm just not Bossuet <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1000604.Jacques_B_nigne_Bossuet">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> , and I hope that my parliament will give strength to those who lack them, and help to regain common sense. It is human to be afraid, but the true value is in mastering fear. That, if you don't do what I do, because if I had it I'd squeal like a pig. So do as I tell you, but not what I do, so we can get something good out of this crisis. Ah, ignore the TVs, who follow the opinions of their sponsors, and lobbyists and who with the coronavirus want to distract you from what is really wrong in the world. Live with caution, but without fear your faith being your strength. Now I apologize to you all, but I thought this little homily needed. This novel "Intensity" was originally. I couldn't find him feet or head. It happened to me as in "The Honesty of Israel Gow" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10313585-the-honesty-of-israel-gow?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=Nf4fJvPox1&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> that it made no sense to me. In fact, I was liking "Nightchills" more (literaryally, I also missed Jenny :-)) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3179866505?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a> I must admit one thing, and it is that the author (Koontz) does not give any respite to the reader, throughout the novel, and that except at first when Laura Templeton, and Chyna are in the car. Except for that moment the rest of the novel is pure horror, brutality, and violence, almost ill-healthy. From Chyna's creepy flashbacks, recalling his terrible childhood. I liked Koontz here in making a denunciation of the sensuous ideologies that led to the degradation of the United States, as a country, as peace and love became a hell, which made a society orphan and without references, t product of this society of peace and love are Ted Bundy and Charles Mason. On this topic read Piers Paul Read's novel "The Professor's Daughter" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/836989.The_Professor_s_Daughter?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=k401ehVKtL&amp;rank=3">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8...</a> Chyna is the product of this destructive spirit embodied by her mother, and her lovers. So Chyna, who is a psychologist, knows what evil is from the beginning, because she has lived it. It's a society of drug addicts, criminals, pedophiles, and people without law and fear of God. From that world he flees, and it seems that he had found refuge, to realize that he is heading for a more terrible fate. What looks like an idyllic family evening leads to carnage. It almost looks like the silent hill video game, fleeing the protagonist of the dark and from a psychopath who initially has more in common with Leatherface, Jason Bateman, Myers and other psychopaths from horror movies. The scenes are harrowing, and I didn't have the feeling that they were well written. At first she was forced to do so, but she didn't understand, because Chyna was trying to follow the killer. It's not bad for Koontz's trick of passing narration from Chyna to psychopath Edgler Vess and vice versa. The psychopath is very well built, and is the product of modern ideologies an empirista, Epicurean, with a moral similar to that of the Marquis of Sade <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2885224.Marquis_de_Sade">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> The good thing about this novel is that it is a mystical Koontz, as my friend Krisi Keley <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4098654.Krisi_Keley">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> warned me is increasingly mystical as Father Brown in "The Equivocal Form", in fact it can be read as a religious allegory in which Chyna is an angel who comes to free Ariel from the demon Vess. In fact, there's an undercover Satanism. If you've read Odd Thomas, you'll see that Vess is very much like Varnet and Eckles, Odd Thomas's Satanist cops, in fact, are cousins. This novel certainly influenced him to make the other. At first he risked falling for "Nightchills" failure to fall into bronsonism or the law of the talion and thought that Miyuki Miyabe in "Crossfire" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14995.Odd_Thomas?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=Sx8nB8KnbK&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/123556.Crossfire?ac=1&amp;from_search=true&amp;qid=PDeLLY4QLd&amp;rank=1">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> The End I liked, and saved Koontz from suspense. He waited for more from Koontz in the future, and to ignore the COUNTRY. Koontz already had strong heroines before Marxism possessed feminism.<br /></span>

    <a title="Jane Stewart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart"><img alt="Jane Stewart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346001994p2/3789528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/359648688?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jane Stewart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jane Stewart" href="/user/show/3789528-jane-stewart">Jane Stewart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780739334256" href="/book/show/21339.Intensity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=suspense-thriller">suspense-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789528-jane-stewart?shelf=5-star-other">5-star-other</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer359648688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2256459538542380111">Fabulous. Scary. Incredible heroine.<br/><br/>Readers who liked The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo should like this. The two heroines (Lisbeth in Dragon Tattoo and Chyna in Intensity) were similar in their actions. Chyna chose to fight what seemed impossible. Instead of running and trying to get away (like normal people) she went after him with the barest of weapons. She was resilient, resourceful, brave. She called it reckless caring. In the beginning of the story, Chyna is trying to get away from Edgler a </span>
  <span id="freeText2256459538542380111" style="display:none">Fabulous. Scary. Incredible heroine.<br /><br />Readers who liked The Girl With The Dragon Tattoo should like this. The two heroines (Lisbeth in Dragon Tattoo and Chyna in Intensity) were similar in their actions. Chyna chose to fight what seemed impossible. Instead of running and trying to get away (like normal people) she went after him with the barest of weapons. She was resilient, resourceful, brave. She called it reckless caring. In the beginning of the story, Chyna is trying to get away from Edgler a serial killer. But when she hears that he has kept a sixteen year old girl prisoner in his basement for a year, Chyna decides to follow him, go to his home, and free the girl. A theme I liked is Lisbeth and Chyna refusing to be victims. In Dragon Tattoo I was scared at times. In Intensity I was scared almost all the time.<br /><br />About a third of the way in I was so scared that I considered stopping unless I had assurance that there would be a good ending. So I jumped to the end and read the last half hour. It was great! The author tied things up well including the aftermath. Then I went back and read the rest of the book. It was still terribly frightening, but I was able to survive because I knew the ending would be good. Reading the end early in no way hurt the story for me. It made it better.<br /><br />Just because I liked this does not mean it’s my preferred genre. I do not want a daily diet of constant scariness and intensity.<br /><br />Edgler enjoyed destroying beauty. He would torture victims with knives and tools. The author does not show the torture/killing scenes in detail. Instead they are told or referred to and the reader sees the bodies after. I was fine with that. But I also would have been ok with more details and gore.<br /><br />A few times Chyna recalls life with her mother Ann. Ann lived a nomadic life with different boyfriends, drinking, and drugs. One boyfriend killed people in Chyna’s presence. Ann enjoyed watching murder. Chyna growing up with Ann was a story of hiding, self protection, and not being cared for. In contrast, I loved the way Chyna treated and cared for Ariel.<br /><br />I love that Koontz does not use tired cliches. He creates his own. They please me. Here are a few examples:<br />She was in an old testament mood, unwilling to turn the other cheek just now.<br />She was baking and nourishing a loaf of panic, plump and yeasty.<br />The car will tumble ass over tea kettle if it goes over the edge.<br /><br />The narrator Kate Burton was fabulous. She used a style so appropriate for the intense sentences with pauses. She enhanced the experience.<br /><br />DATA:<br />Narrative mode: third person. Unabridged audiobook reading time: 11 hrs and 35 mins. Swearing language: (rarely used) strong including religious swear words. Sexual content: one scene vaguely described, no details. Setting: current day California and Oregon. Book copyright: 1995. Genre: suspense thriller. Ending: good guys win.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401514284" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer18248788211641537045">I have never considered Intensity among my favorite Dean Koontz books, but it is a beautiful story. There is very little supernatural element to this one.<a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[my favorite part is the female elk which are portrayed as mysterious guardian angels - really the only supernatural element - so you can see what attracts me to Koontz stories :-)<br/><br/>"The elk's heart-shaped face was barely visible from a distance of only eight feet. It's eyes, however, shone." <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/>I love the references to </span>
  <span id="freeText18248788211641537045" style="display:none">I have never considered Intensity among my favorite Dean Koontz books, but it is a beautiful story. There is very little supernatural element to this one.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[my favorite part is the female elk which are portrayed as mysterious guardian angels - really the only supernatural element - so you can see what attracts me to Koontz stories :-)<br /><br />"The elk's heart-shaped face was barely visible from a distance of only eight feet. It's eyes, however, shone." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I love the references to several classic works of childrens fantasy such as Narnia, Frog &amp; Toad, Alice in Wonderland, Oz etc. Chyna uses these stories (as well as her mantra) to cope through her ordeal.<br /><br />These great closing lines summarize the story:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["How scared Chyna had been that night, risking so much for a girl she had never seen. Scared less of Vess than of this new thing that she had found in herself. This reckless caring. And now she knows it is nothing that should have frightened her. It is the purpose for which we exist. This reckless caring." <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Other favorite passages:<br /><i>The cool air was redolent with the pleasant fecund smell of freshly plowed earth, and there was a sense of mystery in the dark fields that she found intriguing, enchanting - but at times disconcerting, as if they were among unseen presences , ancient spirits that were not all benign.<br />______<br /> <br />It sounded as if someone were opening a giant door in the wall of the night itself and stepping in from another world.<br />______<br /><br />One of the knives was near her hand. It was a table knife with a finely serrated edge, suitable for spreading butter or for slicing well-cooked chicken or for cutting green beans into bite-sized pieces, but not idea for stabbing someone to death.<br />______<br /><br />To the north, left, the highway climbed into a forested night, toward ragged moon-frosted clouds and stars, as if it was a ramp that would carry them right off the planet and up into deepest space.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="18248788211641537045" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696101903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9221050126243730930">In Intensity, Dean Koontz goes from zero to sixty & doesn’t let up, whether it’s an action scene or racing thoughts from the minds of two crazy ass people...it just doesn’t let up, creating an extremely intense experience. I had to listen to this in small doses at certain points. He definitely succeeded in creating an unsettling atmosphere. Unfortunately, in order for him to keep that pace up, we are stuck in the minds of these two and there’s a ton of unnecessary inner dialogue that I could’ve </span>
  <span id="freeText9221050126243730930" style="display:none">In Intensity, Dean Koontz goes from zero to sixty &amp; doesn’t let up, whether it’s an action scene or racing thoughts from the minds of two crazy ass people...it just doesn’t let up, creating an extremely intense experience. I had to listen to this in small doses at certain points. He definitely succeeded in creating an unsettling atmosphere. Unfortunately, in order for him to keep that pace up, we are stuck in the minds of these two and there’s a ton of unnecessary inner dialogue that I could’ve done without. There’s so many problems with the book, if you try to read, rate &amp; review it like a traditional thriller, it will most definitely fall short. However, if you take it for what is, straight-up pulp fiction, with a cat-and-mouse plot between a Final Girl protagonist and a sadistic serial killer...(you literary have to throw out all the rules of what should work)...you might find yourself having fun with it like I did. ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️</span>
  <a data-text-id="9221050126243730930" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2824505266" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2824505266" />
    <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas"><img alt="Benjamin Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451660582p2/4209082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2824505266?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Thomas" href="/user/show/4209082-benjamin-thomas">Benjamin Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345533371" href="/book/show/12467509-intensity">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4209082-benjamin-thomas?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2824505266" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15829807914754626517">Chyna is a 26-year old graduate student of psychology who, due to a traumatic childhood, is just now getting to a point of enjoying what life has to offer. But while taking a short vacation with her best friend in the Napa Valley, she comes face-to-face with a psycho serial killer. Literally, the entire book (after the opening scene) is her attempts to get away from him and/or kill him.<br/><br/>Dean Koontz is always a tough sell for me. Some of his books have been good experiences but others are a real c</span>
  <span id="freeText15829807914754626517" style="display:none">Chyna is a 26-year old graduate student of psychology who, due to a traumatic childhood, is just now getting to a point of enjoying what life has to offer. But while taking a short vacation with her best friend in the Napa Valley, she comes face-to-face with a psycho serial killer. Literally, the entire book (after the opening scene) is her attempts to get away from him and/or kill him.<br /><br />Dean Koontz is always a tough sell for me. Some of his books have been good experiences but others are a real chore to get through. I chose to read this one, basically because it had been sitting on my shelf for a number of years, ever since I bought it at a garage sale for a dime. I was tired of looking at “that yellow Dean Koontz book”.<br /><br />It started off, unfortunately in a bad way with caricatures instead of characters and a rather standard ho-hum plot. Several times, I almost tossed it into the DNF category. The main character, Chyna, was making all the dumb mistakes that they do in cheap horror movies and I was worried the whole book would be like that. Just when she got to where she had a chance to escape, she got distracted by something, to drag things out. She even paused to wash her hands and face at one point instead of running at high speed to get out of the house. <br /><br />There were also way too many times when there were lengthy philosophical meanderings by both Chyna, and the psycho killer. Often these occurred right when the <i>intensity</i> is at its highest. This really interrupts the building suspense…and it happens over and over. The prose itself was dragging things out with long paragraphs describing the tiniest details, usually in repetitive ways. I think this was supposed to be building suspense but I just found it annoying.<br /> <br />I kept at it though and, happily, the second half was much better. When Chyna finally meets the killer and they talk…it all gets pretty interesting and the novel turns into a page turner as Chyna works to escape the killer as well as a pack of his trained Dobermans. But even then, Chyna gets distracted and wastes time when I would have been hauling ass to get away.<br /><br />So, in the end, I have mixed feelings about this one. 3-stars and I’m probably being generous.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15829807914754626517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1085667318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer475722856665312807"><b>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18618986-intensity-mini-group-read-2017' rel='nofollow noopener'>INTENSITY (Mini-Group Read 2017) link - June 1st</a>
</b><br/><br/> This is my second read & I added more "fire" notes. Sheriff Vess is "sick" killing his parents, grandmother & adoptive parents by "fire". In the end, Chyna/Ariel in the motor home chase/crash into Vess' police car & spilled gasoline on the pavement. They roll in gas trying to escape. Chyme reaches to Vess' gas-soaked boots with a <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[butane lighter to light the boots & kill Vess with his <b>sickness with "fire"</b> <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br/><br/><u>
  <b>May 20</b></u></span>
  <span id="freeText475722856665312807" style="display:none"><b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18618986-intensity-mini-group-read-2017" rel="nofollow noopener">INTENSITY (Mini-Group Read 2017) link - June 1st</a>
</b><br><br> This is my second read &amp; I added more "fire" notes. Sheriff Vess is "sick" killing his parents, grandmother &amp; adoptive parents by "fire". In the end, Chyna/Ariel in the motor home chase/crash into Vess' police car &amp; spilled gasoline on the pavement. They roll in gas trying to escape. Chyme reaches to Vess' gas-soaked boots with a <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[butane lighter to light the boots &amp; kill Vess with his <b>sickness with "fire"</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u>
  <b>May 2015</b>
</u> - <i>Many good "intense" escape &amp; thriller sequences are written. Chyna Shepherd (26) finds Laura Templeton (Chyna's best friend) and her family murdered by a psychopath "Serriff" Edger Vess (33). She follows Vess to Ariel Delaney (16) being held captive. Typical hero &amp; chase story with Chyna saving Ariel &amp; taking "care" of Vess. Follow the problems Vess had with the Tempton &amp; Delaney families. Some "intense" scenes are fighting Doberman dogs with ammonia spray &amp; Vess' motor home chases.</i><br><br><blockquote>
<br><b><a href="https://www.imdb.com/title/tt0118350/" rel="nofollow noopener">IMDb Intensity (1997) TV Movie</a></b> <br><b><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nuh3zzjhXl8" rel="nofollow noopener">Intensity TV Trailer (1977 - violent)</a></b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1547453293i/26913828._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>
</blockquote><br>Audio on YouTube.com - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=kbBjlOy1lI0">https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=kbBjlOy...</a></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_32430'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32430.The_Bad_Place"><img alt="The Bad Place" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1388294158l/32430._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g9dthTGysevVg3yxDeBhUZH0l/5H6dV5HSBEvXjYmt658QRXiux4g3KoyND6FWuOR6twNolkWx5GXgIMtZtoRA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
